      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Channel_Islands">
        Channel Islands
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Channel Islands">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helier" title="Saint Helier">
         Saint Helier
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">
         Jersey
        </a>
        : 28,310 inhabitants
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter_Port" title="Saint Peter Port">
         Saint Peter Port
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">
         Guernsey
        </a>
        : 16,488 inhabitants
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Saint_Anne,_Alderney" title="Saint Anne, Alderney">
         Saint Anne, Alderney
        </a>
        : 2,200 inhabitants
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Sark" title="Sark">
         Sark
        </a>
        : 600 inhabitants
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Herm" title="Herm">
         Herm
        </a>
        : 60 inhabitants
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Shipping">
        Shipping
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Shipping">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AIS_Manche_Est.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="455" data-file-width="920" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/AIS_Manche_Est.png/220px-AIS_Manche_Est.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/AIS_Manche_Est.png/330px-AIS_Manche_Est.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/AIS_Manche_Est.png/440px-AIS_Manche_Est.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AIS_Manche_Est.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automatic_Identification_System" title="Automatic Identification System">
          Automatic Identification System
         </a>
         display showing traffic in the Channel in 2006
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Channel has traffic on both the UK-Europe and North Sea-Atlantic routes, and is the world's busiest seaway, with over 500 ships per day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Following an accident in January 1971 and a series of disastrous collisions with wreckage in February,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the Dover TSS
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the world's first
       <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">
        radar
       </a>
       -controlled
       <a href="/wiki/Traffic_Separation_Scheme" title="Traffic Separation Scheme">
        Traffic Separation Scheme
       </a>
       was set up by the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Maritime_Organization" title="International Maritime Organization">
        International Maritime Organization
       </a>
       . The scheme mandates that vessels travelling north must use the French side, travelling south the English side. There is a separation zone between the two lanes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 2002 the
       <a href="/wiki/MV_Tricolor" title="MV Tricolor">
        MV
        <i>
         Tricolor
        </i>
       </a>
       , carrying £30m of luxury cars sank 32 km (20 mi) northwest of Dunkirk after collision in fog with the container ship
       <i>
        Kariba
       </i>
       . The cargo ship
       <i>
        Nicola
       </i>
       ran into the wreckage the next day. There was no loss of life.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2008)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The shore-based long range traffic control system was updated in 2003 and there is a series of Traffic Separation Systems in operation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Though the system is inherently incapable of reaching the levels of safety obtained from aviation systems such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traffic_Collision_Avoidance_System" title="Traffic Collision Avoidance System">
        Traffic Collision Avoidance System
       </a>
       , it has reduced accidents to one or two per year.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2008)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Marine
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPS" title="GPS">
        GPS
       </a>
       systems allow ships to be preprogrammed to follow navigational channels accurately and automatically, further avoiding risk of running aground, but following the fatal collision between Dutch Aquamarine and Ash in October 2001, Britain's
       <a href="/wiki/Marine_Accident_Investigation_Branch" title="Marine Accident Investigation Branch">
        Marine Accident Investigation Branch
       </a>
       (MAIB) issued a safety bulletin saying it believed that in these most unusual circumstances GPS use had actually contributed to the collision.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The ships were maintaining a very precise automated course, one directly behind the other, rather than making use of the full width of the traffic lanes as a human navigator would.
      </p>
      <p>
       A combination of radar difficulties in monitoring areas near cliffs, a failure of a CCTV system, incorrect operation of the anchor, the inability of the crew to follow standard procedures of using a GPS to provide early warning of the ship dragging the anchor and reluctance to admit the mistake and start the engine led to the MV
       <i>
        Willy
       </i>
       running aground in Cawsand bay,
       <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">
        Cornwall
       </a>
       in January 2002. The MAIB report makes it clear that the harbour controllers were informed of impending disaster by shore observers before the crew were themselves aware.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The village of
       <a href="/wiki/Kingsand" title="Kingsand">
        Kingsand
       </a>
       was evacuated for three days because of the risk of explosion, and the ship was stranded for 11 days.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">
        Ecology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ecology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       As a busy shipping lane, the Channel experiences environmental problems following accidents involving ships with toxic cargo and oil spills.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Indeed, over 40% of the UK incidents threatening pollution occur in or very near the Channel.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One of the recent occurrences was the
       <a href="/wiki/MSC_Napoli" title="MSC Napoli">
        MSC
        <i>
         Napoli
        </i>
       </a>
       , which on 18 January 2007 was beached with nearly 1700 tonnes of dangerous cargo in Lyme Bay, a protected World Heritage Site coastline.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The ship had been damaged and was en route to
       <a href="/wiki/Portland_Harbour" title="Portland Harbour">
        Portland Harbour
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
        Transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baie-du-Havre_14_07_2005.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="435" data-file-width="1570" height="61" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Baie-du-Havre_14_07_2005.jpg/220px-Baie-du-Havre_14_07_2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Baie-du-Havre_14_07_2005.jpg/330px-Baie-du-Havre_14_07_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Baie-du-Havre_14_07_2005.jpg/440px-Baie-du-Havre_14_07_2005.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baie-du-Havre_14_07_2005.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The beach of Le Havre and a part of the rebuilt city
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ferry">
        Ferry
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ferry">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Channel_Ports" title="Channel Ports">
        Channel Ports
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The number of ferry routes crossing the
       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Dover" title="Strait of Dover">
        Strait of Dover
       </a>
       has reduced since the
       <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">
        Channel Tunnel
       </a>
       opened. Current cross-channel ferry routes are:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Dover" title="Port of Dover">
         Dover
        </a>
        –
        <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">
         Calais
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Dover–
        <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk" title="Dunkirk">
         Dunkirk
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Newhaven,_East_Sussex" title="Newhaven, East Sussex">
         Newhaven
        </a>
        –
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dieppe,_Seine-Maritime" title="Dieppe, Seine-Maritime">
         Dieppe
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">
         Plymouth
        </a>
        –
        <a href="/wiki/Roscoff" title="Roscoff">
         Roscoff
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Poole" title="Poole">
         Poole
        </a>
        –
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cherbourg" title="Cherbourg">
         Cherbourg
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Poole–
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Malo" title="Saint Malo">
         Saint Malo
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">
         Portsmouth
        </a>
        –Cherbourg
       </li>
       <li>
        Portsmouth–
        <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">
         Jersey
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">
         Guernsey
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Portsmouth–
        <a href="/wiki/Le_Havre" title="Le Havre">
         Le Havre
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Portsmouth–
        <a href="/wiki/Ouistreham" title="Ouistreham">
         Ouistreham
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Portsmouth–Saint Malo
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Rosslare_Europort" title="Rosslare Europort">
         Rosslare
        </a>
        –Cherbourg
       </li>
       <li>
        Rosslare–Roscoff
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Weymouth,_Dorset" title="Weymouth, Dorset">
         Weymouth
        </a>
        –Saint Malo
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Channel_Tunnel">
        Channel Tunnel
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Channel Tunnel">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">
        Channel Tunnel
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Many travellers cross beneath the Channel using the Channel Tunnel, first proposed in the early 19th century and finally opened in 1994, connecting the UK and France by rail. It is now routine to travel between Paris or
       <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">
        Brussels
       </a>
       and London on the
       <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">
        Eurostar
       </a>
       train. Freight trains also use the tunnel. Cars, coaches and lorries are carried on
       <a href="/wiki/Eurotunnel_Shuttle" title="Eurotunnel Shuttle">
        Eurotunnel Shuttle
       </a>
       trains between
       <a href="/wiki/Folkestone" title="Folkestone">
        Folkestone
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">
        Calais
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tourism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Le_Mont_Saint-Michel.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4666" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Le_Mont_Saint-Michel.jpg/220px-Le_Mont_Saint-Michel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Le_Mont_Saint-Michel.jpg/330px-Le_Mont_Saint-Michel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Le_Mont_Saint-Michel.jpg/440px-Le_Mont_Saint-Michel.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Le_Mont_Saint-Michel.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Mont_Saint-Michel" title="Mont Saint-Michel">
          Mont Saint-Michel
         </a>
         is one of the most visited and recognisable landmarks on the English Channel.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The coastal resorts of the Channel, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Brighton" title="Brighton">
        Brighton
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Deauville" title="Deauville">
        Deauville
       </a>
       , inaugurated an era of aristocratic tourism in the early 19th century, which developed into the seaside tourism that has shaped resorts around the world.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Short trips across the Channel for leisure purposes are often referred to as
       <a href="/wiki/Booze_cruise" title="Booze cruise">
        Channel Hopping
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_languages">
        Culture and languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture and languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Norman_dictionary_1779_Kelham.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1638" data-file-width="908" height="307" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Norman_dictionary_1779_Kelham.jpg/170px-Norman_dictionary_1779_Kelham.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Norman_dictionary_1779_Kelham.jpg/255px-Norman_dictionary_1779_Kelham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Norman_dictionary_1779_Kelham.jpg/340px-Norman_dictionary_1779_Kelham.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Norman_dictionary_1779_Kelham.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Kelham's
         <i>
          Dictionary of the Norman or Old French Language
         </i>
         (1779), defining
         <a href="/wiki/Law_French" title="Law French">
          Law French
         </a>
         , a language historically used in English law courts
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The two dominant cultures are English on the north shore of the Channel, French on the south. However, there are also a number of minority languages that are or were found on the shores and islands of the English Channel, which are listed here, with the Channel's name following them.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Celtic Languages
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">
         Breton
        </a>
        – "Mor Breizh" (Sea of Brittany)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">
         Cornish
        </a>
        – "Mor Bretannek"
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">
         Irish
        </a>
        :
        <i>
         <span lang="ga" xml:lang="ga">
          Muir nIocht
         </span>
        </i>
        – "Merciful Sea"
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Germanic languages
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        English
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">
         Dutch
        </a>
        – "het Kanaal" (the Channel)
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Dutch previously had a larger range, and extended into parts of modern-day France. For more information, please see
       <a href="/wiki/French_Flemish" title="French Flemish">
        French Flemish
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Romance languages
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        French – "La Manche"
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Gallo_language" title="Gallo language">
         Gallo
        </a>
        – "Manche", "Grand-Mè", "Mè Bertone"
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-matao_68-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-matao-68">
          [68]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Norman_language" title="Norman language">
         Norman
        </a>
        , including the Channel Island vernaculars:
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Norman_language" title="Anglo-Norman language">
           Anglo-Norman
          </a>
          (extinct, but fossilised in certain English law phrases)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Auregnais" title="Auregnais">
           Auregnais
          </a>
          (extinct)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Cotentinais" title="Cotentinais">
           Cotentinais
          </a>
          – "Maunche"
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guernesiais" title="Guernesiais">
           Guernesiais
          </a>
          – "Ch'nal"
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A8rriais" title="Jèrriais">
           Jèrriais
          </a>
          – "Ch'na"
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sercquais" title="Sercquais">
           Sercquais
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Picard_language" title="Picard language">
         Picard
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Most other languages tend towards variants of the French and English forms, but notably
       <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">
        Welsh
       </a>
       has "Môr Udd".
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Channel_crossings">
        Channel crossings
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Channel crossings">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            verification
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (January 2013)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       As one of the narrowest and most well-known international waterways lacking dangerous currents, the Channel has been the first objective of numerous innovative sea, air, and
       <a href="/wiki/Human_power" title="Human power">
        human powered
       </a>
       crossing technologies.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Pre-historic people sailed from the mainland to England for millennia. At the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">
        last Ice Age
       </a>
       , lower sea levels even permitted
       <a href="/wiki/Doggerland" title="Doggerland">
        walking across
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usask_70-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-usask-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="By_boat">
        By boat
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: By boat">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th width="110pt">
         Date
        </th>
        <th style="text-align:left">
         Crossing
        </th>
        <th style="text-align:left">
         Participant(s)
        </th>
        <th style="text-align:left">
         Notes
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         March 1816
        </td>
        <td>
         The French paddle steamer
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Steam_ship_%C3%89lise" title="Steam ship Élise">
           Élise
          </a>
         </i>
         (ex Scottish-built Margery or Margory) was the first steamer to cross the Channel.
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         9 May 1816
        </td>
        <td>
         Paddle steamer
         <i>
          Defiance
         </i>
         , Captain William Wager, was the first steamer to cross the Channel to Holland
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mariner_Mirror_71-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Mariner_Mirror-71">
           [71]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         10 June 1821
        </td>
        <td>
         Paddle steamer
         <i>
          Rob Roy
         </i>
         , first passenger ferry to cross channel
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         The steamer was purchased subsequently by the French postal administration and renamed
         <i>
          Henri IV
         </i>
         .
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         June 1843
        </td>
        <td>
         First ferry connection through Folkestone-Boulogne
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         Commanding officer
         <a href="/wiki/Captain_Hayward" title="Captain Hayward">
          Captain Hayward
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         25 July 1959
        </td>
        <td>
         Hovercraft crossing (Calais to Dover, 2 hours 3 minutes)
        </td>
        <td>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SR-N1" title="SR-N1">
          SR-N1
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Cockerell" title="Christopher Cockerell">
          Sir Christopher Cockerell
         </a>
         was on board
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         1960s
        </td>
        <td>
         First crossing by
         <a href="/wiki/Water_skiing" title="Water skiing">
          water ski
         </a>
         .
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
         An annual cross-channel ski race was run from the Varne Boat Club from the 1960s onwards. The race was from the Varne club in Greatstone on Sea to Cap Gris Nez / Boulogne (latter years) and back. Many waterskiers have made this return crossing non-stop since this time.
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
             citation needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
         Youngest known waterskier to cross the Channel was John Clements aged 10, from the Varne Boat Club on 22 August 1974 who made the crossing from Littlestone to Boulogne and back without falling.
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">
             citation needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         22 August 1972
        </td>
        <td>
         First solo hovercraft crossing (same route as SR-N1; 2 hours 20 minutes)
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
          <a href="#cite_note-72">
           [72]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         Nigel Beale (UK)
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         1974
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Coracle" title="Coracle">
          Coracle
         </a>
         (13 and a half hours)
        </td>
        <td>
         Bernard Thomas (UK)
        </td>
        <td>
         As part of a publicity stunt, the journey was undertaken to demonstrate how the Bull Boats of the Mandan Indians of North Dakota could have been copied from Welsh coracles introduced by Prince Madog in the 12th century.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
          <a href="#cite_note-73">
           [73]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         14 September 1995
        </td>
        <td>
         Fastest crossing by
         <a href="/wiki/Hovercraft" title="Hovercraft">
          hovercraft
         </a>
         , 22 minutes by
         <i>
          Princess Anne
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         MCH SR-N4 MkIII
        </td>
        <td>
         Craft was designed as a ferry
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         1997
        </td>
        <td>
         First vessel to complete a
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar-power" title="Solar-power">
          solar-powered
         </a>
         crossing using
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_cell" title="Photovoltaic cell">
          photovoltaic cells
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         SB
         <i>
          Collinda
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         —
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         14 June 2004
        </td>
        <td>
         New record time for crossing in amphibious vehicle (the
         <a href="/wiki/Gibbs_Aquada" title="Gibbs Aquada">
          Gibbs Aquada
         </a>
         , three-seater open-top
         <a href="/wiki/Sports_car" title="Sports car">
          sports car
         </a>
         )
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">
          Richard Branson
         </a>
         (UK)
        </td>
        <td>
         Completed crossing in 1 hour 40 minutes 6 seconds – previous record was 6 hours.
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">
             citation needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         26 July 2006
        </td>
        <td>
         New record time for crossing in
         <a href="/wiki/Hydrofoil" title="Hydrofoil">
          hydrofoil
         </a>
         car (the
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rinspeed_Splash&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rinspeed Splash (page does not exist)">
          Rinspeed Splash
         </a>
         , two-seater open-top
         <a href="/wiki/Sports_car" title="Sports car">
          sports car
         </a>
         )
        </td>
        <td>
         Frank M. Rinderknecht (Switzerland)
        </td>
        <td>
         Completed crossing in 3 hours 14 minutes
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         25 September 2006
        </td>
        <td>
         First crossing on a towed inflatable object (not a powered
         <a href="/wiki/Inflatable_boat" title="Inflatable boat">
          inflatable boat
         </a>
         )
        </td>

         Stephen Preston (UK)
        </td>

         Completed crossing in 180 min
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">

          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         July 2007
        </td>
        <td>
         BBC
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Top_Gear_(2002_TV_Series)" title="Top Gear (2002 TV Series)">
          Top Gear
         </a>
         presenters "drive" to France in amphibious cars
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Clarkson" title="Jeremy Clarkson">
          Jeremy Clarkson
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Richard_Hammond" title="Richard Hammond">
          Richard Hammond
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/James_May" title="James May">
          James May
         </a>
         (UK)
        </td>

         Completed the crossing in a 1996
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nissan_Hardbody_Truck" title="Nissan Hardbody Truck">
          Nissan D21
         </a>
         pick-up (the "Nissank"), fitted with a Honda outboard engine.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imcdb.org_76-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-imcdb.org-76">
           [76]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         20 August 2011
        </td>
        <td>
         First Crossing by
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sea_Scooters&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sea Scooters (page does not exist)">
          Sea Scooters
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         A four-man relay team from Scarborough, North Yorkshire, headed by Heath Samples, crossed from Shakespeare Beach to Wissant.
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">
             citation needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         It took 12 hours 26 minutes 39 seconds and set a new Guinness World Record.
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Pierre Andriel crossed the English Channel aboard the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Steam_ship_%C3%89lise" title="Steam ship Élise">
         Élise
        </a>
       </i>
       , ex the Scottish p.s. "Margery" in March 1816, one of the earliest seagoing voyages by
       <a href="/wiki/Steamboat" title="Steamboat">
        steam ship
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The paddle steamer
       <i>
        Defiance
       </i>
       , Captain William Wager, was the first steamer to cross the Channel to Holland, arriving there on 9 May 1816.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mariner_Mirror_71-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mariner_Mirror-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 10 June 1821, English-built
       <a href="/wiki/Paddle_steamer" title="Paddle steamer">
        paddle steamer
       </a>
       <i>
        Rob Roy
       </i>
       was the first passenger ferry to cross channel. The steamer was purchased subsequently by the French postal administration and renamed
       <i>
        Henri IV
       </i>
       and put into regular passenger service a year later. It was able to make the journey across the Straits of Dover in around three hours.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In June 1843, because of difficulties with Dover harbour, the South Eastern Railway company developed the
       <a href="/wiki/Boulogne-sur-Mer" title="Boulogne-sur-Mer">
        Boulogne-sur-Mer
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Folkestone" title="Folkestone">
        Folkestone
       </a>
       route as an alternative to Calais-Dover. The first ferry crossed under the command of
       <a href="/wiki/Captain_Hayward" title="Captain Hayward">
        Captain Hayward
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1974 a Welsh coracle piloted by Bernard Thomas of Llechryd crossed the English Channel to France in 13½ hours. The journey was undertaken to demonstrate how the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bull_Boat" title="Bull Boat">
        Bull Boats
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mandan" title="Mandan">
        Mandan
       </a>
       Indians of
       <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">
        North Dakota
       </a>
       could have been copied from coracles introduced by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Madog" title="Prince Madog">
        Prince Madog
       </a>
       in the 12th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountbatten_class_hovercraft" title="Mountbatten class hovercraft">
        Mountbatten class hovercraft
       </a>
       (MCH) entered commercial service in August 1968, initially between Dover and Boulogne but later also
       <a href="/wiki/Ramsgate" title="Ramsgate">
        Ramsgate
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Pegwell_Bay" title="Pegwell Bay">
        Pegwell Bay
       </a>
       ) to Calais. The journey time Dover to Boulogne was roughly 35 minutes, with six trips per day at peak times. The fastest crossing of the English Channel by a commercial car-carrying hovercraft was 22 minutes, recorded by the
       <i>
        Princess Anne
       </i>
       MCH SR-N4 Mk3 on 14 September 1995,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="By_air">
        By air
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: By air">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_Channel_crossings_by_air" title="List of English Channel crossings by air">
        List of English Channel crossings by air
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first aircraft to cross the Channel was a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balloon_(aircraft)" title="Balloon (aircraft)">
        balloon
       </a>
       in 1785, piloted by
       <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Blanchard" title="Jean-Pierre Blanchard">
        Jean Pierre François Blanchard
       </a>
       (France) and
       <a href="/wiki/John_Jeffries" title="John Jeffries">
        John Jeffries
       </a>
       (US).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB_82-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EB-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Louis_Bl%C3%A9riot" title="Louis Blériot">
        Louis Blériot
       </a>
       (France) piloted the first airplane to cross in 1909.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="By_swimming">
        By swimming
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: By swimming">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_successful_English_Channel_swimmers" title="List of successful English Channel swimmers">
        List of successful English Channel swimmers
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The sport of Channel swimming traces its origins to the latter part of the 19th century when Captain
       <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Webb" title="Matthew Webb">
        Matthew Webb
       </a>
       made the first observed and unassisted swim across the Strait of Dover, swimming from England to France on 24–25 August 1875 in 21 hours 45 minutes.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1927, at a time when fewer than ten swimmers (including the first woman,
       <a href="/wiki/Gertrude_Ederle" title="Gertrude Ederle">
        Gertrude Ederle
       </a>
       in 1926) had managed to emulate the feat and many dubious claims were being made, the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_Swimming_Association&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Channel Swimming Association (page does not exist)">
        Channel Swimming Association
       </a>
       (CSA) was founded to authenticate and ratify swimmers' claims to have swum the Channel and to verify crossing times. The CSA was dissolved in 1999 and was succeeded by two separate organisations:
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=CSA_(Ltd)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="CSA (Ltd) (page does not exist)">
        CSA (Ltd)
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_Swimming_and_Piloting_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Channel Swimming and Piloting Federation (page does not exist)">
        Channel Swimming and Piloting Federation
       </a>
       (CSPF). Both observe and authenticate cross-Channel swims in the Strait of Dover. The Channel Crossing Association was set up at about this time to cater for unorthodox crossings.
      </p>
      <p>
       The team with the most number of Channel swims to its credit is the Serpentine Swimming Club in London,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       followed by the International
       <a href="/wiki/Sri_Chinmoy" title="Sri Chinmoy">
        Sri Chinmoy
       </a>
       Marathon Team.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       By the end of 2005, 811 people had completed 1,185 verified crossings under the rules of the CSA, the CSA (Ltd), the CSPF and Butlins.
      </p>
      <p>
       The number of swims conducted under and ratified by the Channel Swimming Association to 2005 was 982 by 665 people. This includes 24 two-way crossings and three three-way crossings.
      </p>
      <p>
       The number of ratified swims to 2004 was 948 by 675 people (456 men, 214 women). There have been 16 two-way crossings (9 by men and 7 by women). There have been three three-way crossings (2 by men and 1 by a woman). (It is unclear whether this last set of data is comprehensive or CSA only.)
      </p>
      <p>
       The Strait of Dover is the busiest stretch of water in the world. It is governed by International Law as described in
       <i>
        Unorthodox Crossing of the Dover Strait Traffic Separation Scheme
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It states: "[In] exceptional cases the French Maritime Authorities may grant authority for unorthodox craft to cross French territorial waters within the Traffic Separation Scheme when these craft set off from the British coast, on condition that the request for authorisation is sent to them with the opinion of the British Maritime Authorities."
      </p>
      <p>
       The CCA, CSA, and CS&amp;PF are the organisations escorting channel swims, because their pilots have the experience, qualifications, and equipment to guarantee the safety of the swimmers they escort.
      </p>
      <p>
       The fastest verified swim of the Channel was by the Australian
       <a href="/wiki/Trent_Grimsey" title="Trent Grimsey">
        Trent Grimsey
       </a>
       on 8 September 2012, in 6 hours 55 minutes,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       beating the previous record set in 2007 by Bulgarian swimmer
       <a href="/wiki/Petar_Stoychev" title="Petar Stoychev">
        Petar Stoychev
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       There may have been some unreported swims of the Channel, by people intent on entering Britain in circumvention of immigration controls. A failed attempt to cross the Channel by two Syrian refugees in October 2014 only came to light when their bodies were later discovered on the shores of the North Sea in Norway and the Netherlands.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="By_car">
        By car
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: By car">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On 16 September 1965, two Amphicars crossed from Dover to Calais.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Wetsuitmen&amp;rft.date=2015&amp;rft.aulast=Fjellberg&amp;rft.aufirst=Anders&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.dagbladet.no%2Fspesial%2Fvatdraktmysteriet%2Feng%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEnglish+Channel">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-89">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-89">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Autocar article entitled Cars Ahoy published 10 December 1965
         </span>
        </li>
       </ol>
